I haven't tried wet shaving yet, but the dry shaving performance is great. It does not miss very many hairs, and it takes me about 3-4 minutes to shave thoroughly. I've owned this shaver for nearly two months now, and I really don't have much to complain about so far. If I had to choose a negative aspect of this shaver, it would be that the stand cleaner operates somewhat loudly so it would be best if you let it run during the day or if your bathroom is far enough away from your bedrooms. If not, you'll be hearing it hum while you're trying to sleep at night. Without question, I gave this shaver 5 stars because it has met or exceeded all of my expectations, and it shaves close enough that most people would never know that I used an electric shaver.

I have to say those who reviewed it before me did well in directing me to this shaver! The shaver itself is outstanding. I have been very impressed with the closeness of the shave from this razor. I do not like to shave, and generally don't shave on my days off unless I absolutely have to. I work 12 hour shifts, so have alternating 3 & 4 day weekends. Needless to say I have some good growth going when it's time to go to work again. I subsequently have to shave on my first day back on duty with a blade razor, as no electric is going to tackle 1/4 inch of course growth. I subsequently shave with a Gillette Mach 3 Turbo on the first day back on duty. I have found that under the jaw line wrapping onto my neck, I still have some rough stubble after shaving with the Mach 3. After I bought this razor, I tried cleaning up that last bit of stubble with the Arc IV and was amazed that it shaved closer than the blade did, and took off the last vestiges of stubble. Amazing! The old Remington advertised shaving as close as a blade, but it never came close. The Arc IV doesn't brag about being as close as a blade, but it should, as it takes off stubble my Mach 3 Turbo is missing! The shave is also a very comfortable one. The screens warm up while shaving, making for a soft warm comfortable shave. A very nice touch making the shaver actually feel pleasant going across your face. I've also had zero issues with razor burn or hair bumps afterward, unlike the old Remington. The length of the shave time is probably a good half minute shorter than with the old Remington as well, and I don't have to contort my skin in every direction like with the Remington. That said pulling it tight in one direction does still help the shaver get closer, but that is the norm for every electric I've ever used. Ultimately I would rate this razors comfort, closeness of shave and quality at a 5 without question. The reason for my 4 rating has nothing to do with the shaver itself, which I rate as outstanding. The charging/cleaning base has given me an error red light twice while cleaning (charging & drying have been fine, only cleaning is giving me an error), and the manual is completely unclear about what the problem is and how to resolve it. I've seen a couple of reviews talking about issues with the cleaning base, and I might have been an unlucky one to get one of the bad bases. Frankly I consider the cleaning base a gimmick anyway. You can wash the razor off under the tap just fine, and you don't have to pay for cleaning solution packs to do it. Ultimately I would recommend this razor with gusto regardless of the gimmicky base, and if you can find this unit as a stand alone without the base and without the extra cost of the base, jump on it! This is an outstanding razor that provides a terrific close and comfortable shave, with or without the base!

  184. I owned a Panasonic Wet/Dry shaver many, many years ago and I loved it - it was small, gave a very close shave, was waterproof, and only cost me about $35. That thing must lasted me about four or five years...maybe more. Wish I still had that one...it did the job exceedingly well. But technology advances, and this shaver certainly reflects that. I've owned this shaver about three weeks and so far, so good. While it comes with the holder that will charge, clean, and dry the shaver, you actually have a lot of choices about how you clean it after using it. When I first purchased it, I was concerned that cleaning it would always require the cleaning stand with solution, etc. but that is not the case. It can be cleaned quickly under a stream of water or with handsoap. I usually clean it by removing the shaving head cover, running that under water, then switching the shaver on to the cleaning mode and running it under the shower water for about 20 seconds. I then (after my shower) drop it into the charging base, select the \\"Dry\\" and \\"Charge\\" modes by toggling through the selections, and let the charging base do the rest. If I'm in a hurry and don't have time to clean it, then I just drop it in the base and select \\"Clean\\" + \\"Dry\\" + \\"Charge.\\" As far as the shaving, it gets pretty darn close. A few techniques help. I find the closeness of the shave about the same with or without shaving cream. Pulling the skin away from the direction it grows (e.g. pull up on your skin near your cheek since your hair points down) helps the shaver get closer. It seems gentle enough on the skin, although I'm still adjusting to it. Probably the biggest drawback is the size of the shaving head, which makes it hard to shave around and above my mustache. I've had to touch up that area with a blade. I'm in the Reserves, so I can't just let my mustache grow wild and spread out across my face. If you're not in that position, then no problem. I think one could shave aroundhis beard without any issues. There is also a pop-out trimmer that seems to work fine, but doesn't trim nearly as close as the shaver head cuts (of course, it's not designed to). Overall, I'm happy with it and having purchased it on sale for $93 with a $20 rebate, I'm sure I've gotten a good value.

  206. Well, first of all, I can say that I've tried several different versions of Norelco up to the Quattro, and I even payed $180 for the first Braun with a cleaning station (though I can't even remember what it was called at this point.) I have a very sensitive neck with problems shaving around my adam's apple even with newer disposable razors or cartridge razors, and after my last infection my doctor told me that I would either have to blow dry my razors clean to reuse them or only use them once. At that point I started to buy the cheapest disposables I could find (which turn out to be Wilkinson's Sword at Walmart; an 8 pack costs just under $6 with the Personna version being 10 cents cheaper but of much lower quality.) I also started to look into another electric razor that cleans itself, and after some research of reviews found the Arc IV's to be the best rated out there. I've had the razor for over 2 weeks now, and the dry cleaning cartridge seems to work much better than Braun's series cartidges; not to mention they are much cheaper. Also, whether or not you use the Braun cartridges, the alcohol based cleaner will evaporate within 2 weeks either way. The Panasonic cleaning cartridges are supposed to last 30 days whether you use them or not, and I've also read that people that don't use them daily can make them last much longer. Also, on the package for the cleaning cartridge, it says that the detergent will stay good for 6 months after opening and I find that another good sign that they will last much longer, giving me the chance to either just rinse the razor after use or use hand soap to clean and just use the drying and charging functions on the station; though I tend to only charge the battery when I get to 10% to preserve the battery. Enough about specs, let's talk about the shave. I've invested some extra money into decent pre and after-shaves. After using the razor dry, I found I still had an unacceptable amount of hair around my neck, and started researching pre-electric lotions. I found Aramis Lab Series pre-electric shave on Amazon, and granted it is rather expensive when compared to Afta or Lectric-Shave, but a little goes a long way, and since I started using it I've had the best shave I've ever had with an electric razor...better than I get with some blades actually. Its so close and smooth that even my wife can't tell that I didn't use a blade razor, and for that I can't be happy enough. I know that the foils have a tendency to break or wear thin on these, but I wouldn't even mind paying for a foil every six months if it continues to shave this close; I'm still saving money over disposables. Also, I invested in some Proraso cream after-shave balm; $16 with free shipping if you have Amazon prime, but so far one of the best after-shaves I've ever used. After shave with the Aramis Lab Series pre-shave, I wash my face and put on a little of the Proraso just to moisturize and heal my skin, and its like I never even shaved at times. I'm also the type of person that will have at least 20 nicks or just abrasion all over after shaving usually, and by using this razor properly I can get a close shave without any of that. So, if you're looking to switch to a good electric razor or maybe just looking to save some money in the long run but don't mind putting up a good bit of money to start out, I would definitely recommend this razor to you. I haven't tried the wet shaving yet because I've read that it tends to clog the razor up, and if you think about how it works that completely makes sense. I'd say invest in a good electric pre-shave and an after shave balm that is good for your skin (takes some experimenting to find the right stuff, but I've seen good stuff about Trumper's Coral Skin Food, Proraso cream after-shave balm, and if you want to go a little cheaper even OTC Nivea Extra-Soothing After Shave Balm, right now I'm still using some 2 year old after shave balm an aunt got me for Christmas from Bathand Body Works, but they don't carry that line any more,) but this is by far the best electric razor I've ever used. I'm almost regretful that I didn't step up to the $200 version on Amazon for the 14,000 rpm over the 13,000 rpm for this one, but it was an $87 difference, and I wasn't even sure if this kind of razor would work good for me at the time. I know what I'll be replacing this one with in a couple years, though. =)

The shave is really close and a single shave for me is around 10% of charge(around 5-6 minutes). The cleaning mode is quieter then my ten year old Braun shaver. I have not used the self cleaning mode, but I will be able to try it out after my trip in March. The only negative I have found is that I cannot find the refill blades or cleaning cartridges locally. The cleaning cartridges are cheaper too if you do the subscribe and save option. The Braun refills are around 10-12 dollars locally where I live. I ordered 4 three packs for a six month renewal and then went into the subscribe and save settings and set it to skip the next 6 month shipment. That way I would get a new years supply ordered next year. I am very happy with this unit!

  308. Summary of pros: Shaves great on a greasy or sweaty face. Cleans quick and effectively Shaves quick and close Summary of cons: Pop-up razor is slightly flimsy This razor works perfectly, and is the best electric razor I've owned so far. Before the Arc IV, I used an electric Braun shaver (don't remember the model, I bought it from costco), which shaved alright under most conditions, but was absolutely useless when my face was greasy or sweaty, and ended up causing me more pain than I'd have liked. Since the Arc IV can be used with shaving gel or on a wet face, it solves the problem. Also, I legitimately think it shaves better when my face is greasy or wet, with or without gel, so I'm very pleased. Another thing I hated about my Braun was its cleaning stations: it was expensive ($5 a month) and absolutely necessary. If I skipped a cleaning and just dusted the hairs out, the grease on the shaver would make the next shave infuriating and painful. The Arc IV is wonderful to clean; because it's waterproof, you just put a little ordinary liquid soap and water on the head, operate the turbo mode, then take it apart and rinse the pieces off under a faucet. The entire cleaning process takes a mere minute from start to finish, and leaves it perfectly clean for the next shave. By the way, it baffles me how waterproof this thing is; it has no problems charging even when there is water on the metal contacts used for charging! I'm very impressed. The only problem (hardly a problem) with cleaning it this way is that you have to lay all of the parts out to dry for a couple of hours; even drying the pieces off with a towel, you cannot immediately recombine the parts because they won't dry correctly. Doing so leaves a kind of rusty smell for the next shave, but the shave is still very good. The last thing I hated about my Braun is the time it took to shave: 5-7 minutes for a good shave, 7-10 for a great shave. Shaving with the Arc IV is ridiculously quick; I can get a pretty good shave in 2.5 minutes (no joke), and a pretty great shave in about 5 minutes. The head of this razor is relatively huge with its 4 blades, which is why the shave is so quick. Probably the only thing I don't like about the Arc IV is its pop-up razor, as it feels a little flimsy and easily pops back down while I am using it. It's not a big deal; I just generally have to be slow and careful when using it. All in all, this is an excellent razor, and I'd easily suggest this to my friends. Stop reading the (enormously positive, and accurate) reviews and just buy it already! You'll be glad you made the decision to switch.
